[4:3:66,152] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES  

[4:4:66,169] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide programmatic support to assist with advocacy, capacity  

[4:5:66,179] building, systems change, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices  

[4:6:66,189] and advisory committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State  

[4:7:66,198] Plan for inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature. These offices also carry out direct service supports  

[4:8:66,208] for pandemic and emergency responses.  

[5:0:66,228] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and  

[5:1:66,238] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community  

[5:2:66,247] facilities:  

[6:0:65,265] • Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative  

[6:1:76,274] to assist them in making choices and decisions.  

[6:2:65,290] • Clients' rights advocacy services to ensure that laws, regulations, and policies pertaining to the rights of persons with  

[6:3:76,300] developmental disabilities are observed.  

[6:4:65,316] • Quality Assessments for individuals who receive community residential services and support.  

[6:5:65,332] • Other efforts and projects related to self-determination and supported decision-making.

[6:0:66,471] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,490] 3820 -  EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES AUTHORITY  

[6:2:66,507] Disaster Medical Services Division  

[7:0:66,525] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the  

[7:1:66,534] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The  

[7:2:66,544] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National  

[7:3:66,554] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals,  

[7:4:66,564] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical  

[7:5:66,573] response in California.  

[7:6:66,591] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division  

[8:0:66,608] The Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active  

[8:1:66,618] paramedics throughout the state. The Division develops and implements regulations that set training, certification and licensure  

[8:2:66,628] standards, and the scope of practice for various emergency medical services personnel. The Division also sets standards for,  

[8:3:66,637] and reviews and approves, training programs in public safety first aid, pediatric first aid, CPR,   preventive health practices for  

[8:4:66,647] child day care providers, and school bus drivers. It also develops standards for pre-arrival emergency care instructions and the  

[8:5:66,657] epinephrine auto-injector training program.  

[8:6:66,674] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division  

[9:0:66,691] The Emergency Medical Services Systems Division is responsible for developing and implementing emergency medical  

[9:1:66,701] services systems throughout California, including the support of local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the  

[9:2:66,711] state to collect more meaningful data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] Division also oversees system development and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the  

[3:1:66,78] statewide trauma system, and emergency medical dispatcher and communication standards.   Additionally, it   establishes  

[3:2:66,88] regulations and guidelines for local agencies; reviews and approves local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state  

[3:3:66,98] standards; coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the California Department of Public Health and the Office of  

[3:4:66,108] Traffic Safety; manages the state's emergency medical services data and quality improvement process; conducts Ambulance  

[3:5:66,117] Exclusive Operating Area evaluations; oversees the operation of California's Poison Control System; and manages the  

[3:6:66,127] Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[2:0:107,32] 4140   Department of Health Care Access and Information - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Hospital Fair Billing Program receives and investigates consumer complaints regarding hospital billing and enforces the  

[3:1:66,78] hospital fair pricing policies. The Office of Health Care Affordability (OHCA) has three primary responsibilities: managing cost  

[3:2:66,88] growth targets, monitoring system performance, and assessing market consolidation. OHCA will collect, analyze, and publicly  

[3:3:66,98] report data on total health care expenditures, and enforce cost growth targets set by a new Health Care Affordability Board. To  

[3:4:66,108] ensure a balanced approach to managing costs, OHCA will monitor system performance by measuring quality, equity, adoption  

[3:5:66,117] of alternative payment models, investment in primary care and behavioral health, and workforce stability. Through cost and  

[3:6:66,127] market impact reviews, OHCA will analyze transactions that are likely to significantly impact on market competition, the state’s  

[3:7:66,137] ability to meet cost targets, or affordability for consumers and purchasers. Based on results of the review, OHCA will then  

[3:8:66,147] coordinate with other state agencies to address consolidation as appropriate.  

[3:9:66,164] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE  

[4:0:66,183] The Health Care Workforce Program improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved  

[4:1:66,193] areas throughout California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that  

[4:2:66,203] provide financial incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program  

[4:3:66,213] promotes health care workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs:  

[4:4:65,230] • Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program  

[5:0:65,246] • Mental Health Services Act Workforce Education and Training Program  

[5:1:65,262] • Health Professions Careers Opportunity Program  

[5:2:65,277] • Health Workforce Pilot Projects Program  

[5:3:65,293] • Health Workforce Research Data Center  

[6:0:65,309] • California Primary Care Office which includes the Shortage Designation Program  

[6:1:65,325] • California State Office of Rural Health includes:  

[6:2:74,342] • The J-1 Visa Waiver Program  

[6:3:74,358] • Small Hospital Improvement Program  

[7:0:74,374] • Medicare Critical Access Hospital Flexibility Program  

[7:1:65,397] • California Health Workforce Education and Training Council  

[7:2:65,413] • Scholarship Programs  

[8:0:65,428] • Loan Repayment Programs, including the California State Loan Repayment Program, Steven M. Thompson Physician Corps  

[8:1:76,438] Loan Repayment Program and Licensed Mental Health Services Provider Education Program  

[8:2:65,454] • Children and Youth Behavioral Health Initiative Workforce Programs  

[8:3:66,471] 3840 - FACILITIES DEVELOPMENT  

[9:0:66,488] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and  

[9:1:66,498] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of  

[9:2:66,508] providing sustained services to the public.  

[9:3:66,525] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE  

[10:0:66,545] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and  

[10:1:66,555] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors  

[10:2:66,564] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating  

[10:3:66,574] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California.  

[10:4:66,591] The Distressed Hospital Loan Program requires HCAI and the California Health Facilities Financing Authority (CHFFA) to  

[10:5:66,601] collaboratively administer the Distressed Hospital Loan Program to offer interest-free, working capital loans to non-profit and  

[10:6:66,611] publicly-operated financially distressed hospitals, including hospitals that belong to integrated health care systems with no more  

[10:7:66,621] than two separately licensed hospitals in California that are facing a risk of closure, while they implement turnaround strategies  

[10:8:66,631] to regain financial viability.   HCAI contracts with CHFFA through an Inter-Agency Agreement to administer the loan program. 

[10:9:66,640] The founding legislation also includes provisions requiring hospitals to submit quarterly financial data to HCAI, for use in  

[10:10:66,650] monitoring the financial health of hospitals throughout the state.  

[10:11:66,667] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[11:0:66,685] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from  

[11:1:66,694] approximately 9,500 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment  

[11:2:66,704] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory  

[11:3:66,714] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers,  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media. To further this  

[3:1:66,78] mission, the Health Care Information Program is implementing new health care cost transparency data programs to collect and  

[3:2:66,88] analyze prescription drug cost data, hospital supplier diversity data, hospital quality and equity data, and health care payment  

[3:3:66,98] data to improve transparency, inform policy decisions, reduce disparities, and reduce health care costs.

[5:0:184,248] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care  

[5:1:66,268] The Department of Managed Health Care protects health care consumers   and ensures a stable health care delivery system in  

[5:2:66,278] California. The Department achieves this mission by:  

[5:3:65,295] • Licensing and regulating the full scope of managed care models, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMO),  

[5:4:76,305] Preferred Provider Organizations (PPO), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPO), Point-of-Service (POS) products and  

[5:5:76,315] Medi-Cal managed care plans. The Department also licenses and conducts financial reviews of Medicare Advantage and  

[5:6:76,325] Part D plans and licenses and regulates specialized health plans including chiropractic, dental, vision, psychological  

[5:7:76,335] (behavioral health) and pharmacy.  

[5:8:65,350] • Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended.  

[5:9:65,366] • Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are  

[5:10:76,376] financially stable to serve their enrollees.  

[5:11:65,392] • Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical  

[5:12:76,401] Review program.  

[5:13:65,417] • Reviewing proposed health plan rate changes for sufficient justification and reasonableness.  

[5:14:65,433] • Monitoring the financial solvency of the medical groups with whom health plans contract to provide health benefits to their  

[5:15:76,443] enrollees.  

[6:0:65,459] • Convening the Financial Solvency Standards Board, comprised of people with expertise in the medical, financial and health  

[6:1:76,468] plan industries, to advise the Director on strategies to keep the managed care industry financially stable.

[7:1:66,397] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,417] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve  

[8:1:66,427] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans,  

[8:2:66,436] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist  

[8:3:66,446] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which

[6:0:198,397] 4170   California Department of Aging  

[7:0:66,418] The Department of Aging's mission is to transform aging for individuals, families, and communities by leading innovative  

[8:0:66,428] programs, planning, policies, and partnerships that increase choices, equity, and well-being for all Californians as we age. The  

[8:1:66,437] population served includes older adults, people with disabilities, and family caregivers.  

[9:0:66,455] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the California Department of Aging (CDA) administers federal Older  

[10:0:66,464] Americans Act programs that provide a wide variety of home and community-based supportive services through contracts with  

[10:1:66,474] a statewide network of 33 Area Agencies on Aging (AAAs) and the 11 statewide Caregiver Resource Centers (CRCs). The  

[11:0:66,484] Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs; it contracts directly with agencies that operate 37 Multipurpose Senior  

[11:1:66,494] Services Program (MSSP) sites and certifies 289 Community-Based Adult Services (CBAS) centers for participation in Medi-

[11:2:66,504] Cal.   In addition, the Department oversees implementation of the Governor’s Master Plan for Aging and California’s efforts to  

[12:0:66,513] build a No Wrong Door system centered in the development of the Aging and Disability Resource Connection (ADRC) program  

[12:1:66,523] to provide person centered counseling and support to older adults, people with disabilities, and family caregivers. CDA  

[13:0:66,533] administers the Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP) that provides individualized counseling to  

[14:0:66,543] Medicare beneficiaries, and houses the State Long-Term Care Ombudsman program with oversight for the rights of residents in  

[14:1:66,552] long-term care facilities.

[6:1:66,682] 3890 - NUTRITION

[7:1:66,710] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:412,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — HHS   31 

[2:0:163,32] 4170   California Department of Aging - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and  

[3:1:66,78] assistance, employment, and education.  

[3:2:66,96] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE  

[4:0:66,115] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized  

[4:1:66,125] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also  

[4:2:66,135] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.  

[4:3:66,152] 3900 - SUPPORTIVE SERVICES  

[5:0:66,171] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers,  

[5:1:66,181] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance,  

[5:2:66,191] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term  

[5:3:66,201] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support  

[5:4:66,211] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care  

[5:5:66,220] services appropriate to their needs.  

[5:6:66,238] CAREGIVER RESOURCE CENTERS  

[6:0:66,255] This program provides support and resources to family caregivers of adults affected by chronic and debilitating health  

[6:1:66,265] conditions, degenerative diseases, or traumatic brain injuries and adults 60 years and older in need of assistance with daily  

[6:2:66,274] living activities such as, bathing, eating, or getting dressed.? There are 11 nonprofit Caregiver Resource Centers that provide  

[6:3:66,284] services in each county.  

[7:0:66,301] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS  

[8:0:66,319] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides  

[8:1:66,329] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local  

[8:2:66,338] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans.  

[8:3:66,356] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS  

[9:0:66,373] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services  

[9:1:66,383] (CBAS) program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social  

[9:2:66,392] care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who  

[9:3:66,402] otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to  

[9:4:66,412] adults 18 years of age or over who are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health  

[9:5:66,422] conditions and/or disabilities. The Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program.  

[9:6:66,439] 3915 - POLICY AND PLANNING  

[10:0:66,456] This program is responsible for Aging policy research, analysis, and development for the State’s Aging programs. The program  

[10:1:66,466] specifically addresses policy and planning related to inclusion and isolation prevention, equity-in-aging, housing and livable  

[10:2:66,476] communities, and health in the home and community.

[11:0:66,516] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[11:1:66,534] 3930 - COMMISSION ON AGING  

[12:0:66,552] The Commission works with the Legislature, government officials and public, nonprofit and private-sector organizations to  

[12:1:66,561] address public policy and issues that impact older Californians. The Commission prepares, publishes and disseminates  

[12:2:66,571] information, findings and recommendations regarding the well-being of older adults, advises the California Department of Aging  

[12:3:66,581] on the development of the State Plan on Aging and monitors Plan implementation. As part of its information-gathering  

[12:4:66,591] responsibility, the Commission holds meetings, forums   and public hearings around the State. The Commission held  

[12:5:66,601] membership on the Governor’s Master Plan for Aging Stakeholder Advisory Committee and currently holds membership on the 

[12:6:66,610] Aging and Disability Resource Connection Advisory Committee, Behavioral Health Task Force,   Disability and Aging Community  

[12:7:66,620] Living Advisory Committee, Elder and Disability Justice Coordinating Council, and the California Aging and Disability Research  

[12:8:66,630] Partnership.   The Commission also provides administrative support for the Area Agency on Aging Advisory Councils of  

[12:9:66,640] California, which is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included on the State income tax

[3:0:66,68] The State Department of Health Care Services' (DHCS) purpose is to provide equitable access to high-quality health care  

[4:0:66,78] leading to a healthy California for all. To fulfill its purpose, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care  

[4:1:66,88] service delivery programs, including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-

[4:2:66,98] income persons and families who meet defined eligibility requirements.

[6:0:66,356] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,374] 3960010 - MEDICAL CARE SERVICES (MEDI-CAL)  

[7:0:66,392] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal  

[7:1:66,401] provides access to high-quality health care services in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed  

[7:2:66,411] care delivery systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following functional groups: Health Care Benefits and  

[7:3:66,421] Eligibility; Health Care Delivery Systems; Health Care Financing; Behavioral Health; Audits and Investigations; Enterprise Data  

[7:4:66,431] and Information Management; and Program Operations.  

[7:5:66,448] 3960023 - CHILDREN'S MEDICAL SERVICES  

[8:0:66,465] Children's Medical Services is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income and  

[8:1:66,475] seriously ill children, including the Genetically Handicapped Persons Program and the California Children's Services Program.  

[8:2:66,492] 3960032 - PRIMARY, RURAL, AND INDIAN HEALTH  

[9:0:66,510] Primary, Rural, and Indian Health is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care to Californians in rural  

[9:1:66,519] areas and to underserved populations through the following programs: Indian Health Program, American Indian Maternal  

[9:2:66,529] Support Services, and Tribal Emergency Preparedness Program.  

[9:3:66,546] 3960050 - OTHER CARE SERVICES  

[10:0:66,564] The Department is also responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of non-Medi-Cal community health services;  

[10:1:66,573] mental health and substance use disorder services; cancer screening services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured  

[10:2:66,583] individuals; and prostate cancer treatment services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured men. These services are  

[10:3:66,593] provided through the   Behavioral Health Community   Services Division, Behavioral Health Licensing and Certification Division,  

[10:4:66,603] the Every Woman Counts Program, and the Prostate Cancer Treatment Program.

[8:1:66,428] through the following core activities:  

[8:2:65,446] • Protecting the public from communicable diseases.  

[8:3:65,461] • Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments, and improving social determinants of health and healthy  

[8:4:76,471] communities.  

[9:0:65,487] • Preventing disease, injury, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities by embedding  

[9:1:76,497] health and mental health equity language, tools, and approaches into all public health and partner agency policies, practices,  

[9:2:76,506] programs, systems, and resource allocation.  

[9:3:65,522] • Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies.  

[9:4:65,538] • Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status; inform people, institutions and communities; and to  

[9:5:76,548] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions.  

[9:6:65,564] • Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces.  

[9:7:65,579] • Providing access to quality, population-based health services.

[7:0:66,481] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,499] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness and Response  

[8:0:66,517] The Emergency Preparedness and Response program provides expertise, leadership, and dedicated support for the  

[8:1:66,526] coordination of emergency planning, preparedness, response, and recovery efforts for all public health emergencies and  

[8:2:66,536] disasters, including natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and infectious diseases. The program oversees statewide public health  

[8:3:66,546] disaster planning; supports medical care and public health systems to plan for and respond to medical surge; coordinates and  

[8:4:66,556] facilitates efforts between federal, state, and local entities; and maintains other risk communications and response systems  

[8:5:66,566] during emergencies and disasters. The program also administers federal and state funds to support public health emergency  

[8:6:66,575] preparedness and response activities at the state and local levels.  

[8:7:66,593] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH  

[9:0:66,610] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic  

[9:1:66,620] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These  

[9:2:66,629] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California.  

[9:3:66,647] 4045010 - Healthy Communities  

[10:0:66,664] The Healthy Communities program works to prevent and control chronic diseases such as cancer, cardiovascular diseases,  

[10:1:66,674] asthma, Alzheimer's, and diabetes; to reduce the prevalence of obesity; to reduce tobacco use; to improve oral health through  

[10:2:66,684] prevention, education, and community efforts; to provide training programs for the public health workforce; to prevent and  

[10:3:66,693] control injuries, violence, deaths, and diseases related to behavioral, environmental, and occupational factors; to promote and  

[10:4:66,703] support safe, equitable, and healthy environments in communities and workplaces; to prevent substance and gambling  

[10:5:66,713] addiction and treat gambling disorder; and to support suicide prevention efforts. This program includes the California Tobacco  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[4:0:66,115] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases  

[5:0:66,132] The Infectious Diseases program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, COVID-19, viral  

[5:1:66,142] hepatitis, influenza and other vaccine-preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections,  

[5:2:66,152] and foodborne illnesses. This program includes the Division of Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of  

[5:3:66,162] Binational Border Health, the Office of Refugee Health, the Office of Guidance and Policy, and the Office of Infectious Disease  

[5:4:66,171] Preparedness and Response.  

[6:0:66,189] 4045032 - Family Health  

[7:0:66,206] The Family Health program works to improve the health and well-being of individuals, pregnant people, children and youth as  

[7:1:66,216] well as reduce disparities in perinatal health outcomes. This program includes the Genetic Disease Screening Program;  

[7:2:66,226] Maternal, Child, and Adolescent Health; and the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and Children.  

[8:0:66,243] 4045041 - Health Statistics and Informatics  

[9:0:66,260] The Health Statistics and Informatics program works to improve the public’s health by managing information systems and  

[9:1:66,270] facilitating the collection, validation, analysis, and dissemination of health statistics and demographic information on the  

[9:2:66,280] California population. This program includes Vital Records and Public Health Informatics.  

[10:0:66,297] 4045050 - County Health Services  

[11:0:66,314] The County Health Services program supports county-based public health information and services, including the Medical  

[11:1:66,324] Marijuana Identification Card Program.  

[12:0:66,341] 4045059 - Environmental Health  

[13:0:66,359] The Environmental Health program works to protect and improve the health of all California residents by utilizing inspection,  

[13:1:66,368] technical assistance, regulatory, investigation, and emergency response activities to improve the safety of foods, industrial  

[13:2:66,378] hemp products, drugs, and medical devices; conduct underage tobacco enforcement; oversee the use of radiation and  

[13:3:66,388] radioactive materials; regulate medical waste; and conduct other environmental management programs. The program includes  

[13:4:66,398] the Division of Food and Drug Safety and the Division of Radiation Safety and Environmental Management.  

[14:0:66,415] 4045068 - Laboratory Sciences  

[15:0:66,432] The Center for Laboratory Sciences   provides laboratory testing services, technical consultation, and leadership for the State's  

[15:1:66,442] Public Health Laboratory System to protect Californians from the threat of infectious and environmental diseases. The   Center  

[15:2:66,452] includes the Drinking Water and   Radiation Laboratory, Environmental Health Laboratory, Food and   Drug Laboratory, Infant  

[15:3:66,461] Botulism Treatment and   Prevention Program, Microbial Diseases Laboratory, and Viral and   Rickettsial   Disease Laboratory. The  

[15:4:66,471] Center   provides laboratory testing services to support public health surveillance programs; research for disease diagnosis,  

[15:5:66,481] characterization, investigation, and control; and subject matter expertise to inform effective decision-making.  

[16:0:66,498] 4050 - LICENSING AND CERTIFICATION  

[17:0:66,516] 4050010 - Health Facilities  

[18:0:66,533] The Health Facilities program regulates the quality of care in over 14,000 public and private health facilities, clinics, and  

[18:1:66,543] agencies throughout the state; licenses nursing home administrators; certifies nurse assistants, home health aides, and  

[18:2:66,552] hemodialysis technicians; and oversees the prevention, surveillance and reporting of healthcare-associated infections in  

[18:3:66,562] California's health facilities.  

[19:0:66,579] 4050019 - Laboratory Field Services  

[20:0:66,597] The Laboratory Field Services program regulates California clinical and public health laboratory, blood bank, biologics, and  

[20:1:66,606] tissue bank quality standards through licensure and oversight of approximately 27,000 clinical laboratories, public health  

[20:2:66,616] laboratories, blood banks, biologics facilities, and tissue banks operating in California; and approximately 77,000 California  

[20:3:66,626] laboratory personnel in more than 30 different categories of laboratory personnel including phlebotomists, cytotechnologists,  

[20:4:66,636] medical laboratory technicians, clinical laboratory scientist trainees, clinical laboratory scientists, public health microbiologists,  

[20:5:66,646] clinical reproductive biologists, bioanalysts, and clinical laboratory directors.  

[21:0:66,663] 9900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[22:0:66,680] This program provides overall management, planning, policy development, and administrative support services for all DPH  

[22:1:66,690] programs. This program is carried out by the Director's Office, the Office of Health Equity, the Office of Compliance, the Office  

[22:2:66,700] of Policy and Planning, the Strategic Development and External Relations Fusion Center, the Office of Communications, the

[2:0:141,32] 4300   Department of Developmental Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Department of Developmental Services (Department) is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities  

[3:1:66,78] Services Act for overseeing the coordination and delivery of services and supports that persons with developmental disabilities  

[3:2:66,88] need to lead more independent and productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets  

[3:3:66,98] broad policy and provides leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities and standards within which  

[3:4:66,108] the developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate  

[3:5:66,117] problems that arise. Services are delivered through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community  

[3:6:66,127] agencies known as regional centers as well as through state-operated programs. The Department, through contracts with the  

[3:7:66,137] 21 regional centers, oversees through audits and other review the coordination of services to persons with developmental  

[3:8:66,147] disabilities; provides that such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these individuals at each  

[3:9:66,156] stage of their lives; and, to the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home community.  

[3:10:66,174] Because the Department’s programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[3:11:66,183] support this need. For specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:141,32] 4300   Department of Developmental Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,87] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,106] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,126] Through the network of regional centers, the Department contracts with regional centers to support the development and  

[5:1:66,136] maintenance of services for eligible persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers  

[5:2:66,145] directly provide or coordinate the following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis,  

[5:3:66,155] (3) counseling, (4) lifelong individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the  

[5:4:66,165] individual program plan, (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of  

[5:5:66,175] legal, civil, and service rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning,  

[5:6:66,184] placement, and monitoring for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families,  

[5:7:66,194] (12) community education about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services.  

[6:0:66,211] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,229] The Department currently operates two larger residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County), which is in  

[7:1:66,239] warm shutdown, and Porterville Developmental Center (Tulare County). Secure treatment services are provided at the  

[7:2:66,248] Porterville Developmental Center for   individuals who have been found incompetent to stand trial due to their developmental  

[7:3:66,258] disability or are dangerous to themselves or others and civilly committed to the facility by court order. The Department also  

[7:4:66,268] operates Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences in Northern, Central, and Southern  

[8:0:66,278] California   to provide acute crisis services in the community. Finally, the Department leases one community facility for persons  

[8:1:66,287] who require specialized behavioral interventions and acute crisis stabilization: Canyon Springs in Cathedral City (Riverside  

[8:2:66,297] County). Under the California Department of Public Health, Porterville Developmental Center is licensed as a General Acute  

[8:3:66,307] Care Hospital and Intermediate Care Facility, and Canyon Springs Community Facility operates as an Intermediate Care  

[8:4:66,317] Facility.  

[9:0:66,334] STAR residences operate as community crisis homes. Services involve the provision of active treatment through residential  

[9:1:66,344] and day programs on a 24-hour basis, including appropriate medical and dental care, health maintenance activities, and  

[9:2:66,354] assistance with activities of daily living, training, education, and employment.  

[10:0:66,371] Individuals served in the STAR crisis   residences are committed by a court order to the Department for suitable treatment and  

[10:1:66,381] habilitation services during a crisis and are provided services and supports necessary to prepare them for return to their home  

[10:2:66,390] or to transition to a new living option. The primary objective of this program   is to provide a safety net of services that include  

[10:3:66,400] providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents based upon assessed need and as outlined in  

[10:4:66,410] each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most efficient, effective, and least restrictive manner  

[10:5:66,420] to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system and are designed to teach individuals the skills for  

[10:6:66,429] increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and welfare, and enhance personal competence in  

[10:7:66,439] all areas of daily living.  

[11:0:66,457] 4149 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION  

[12:0:66,476] The objective of this program is to: (1) provide overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[12:1:66,486] and administrative services; (2) manage revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[12:2:66,496] companies, and private payers; (3) monitor regional center operations for compliance with statute, regulations, and their  

[12:3:66,505] contract with the Department; (4) provide central administrative and clinical management services to the   state-operated  

[12:4:66,515] programs to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with state licensing and federal certification requirements,  

[12:5:66,525] protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures and grounds; and (5) oversee areas that include the  

[12:6:66,535] development of policies and procedures for developmental center operations, law enforcement and protective services,

[5:0:66,153] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[6:0:66,172] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible for the operation and maintenance of facilities under its control,  

[6:1:66,181] including two state-owned and operated 24-hour care facilities and related buildings, grounds, and infrastructure. The facilities  

[6:2:66,191] are Fairview Developmental Center in Orange County and Porterville Developmental Center in Tulare County.  

[6:3:66,208] The developmental centers are comprised of approximately 2.3 million gross square feet on 784 acres. As of February 2020,  

[6:4:66,218] the Fairview Developmental Center and the Porterville General Treatment Area transitioned all former residents to community  

[6:5:66,228] living. The Department will continue to maintain the Fairview property in warm shutdown mode until disposition of the property.  

[6:6:66,238] The Department is projected to operate seven Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences that  

[6:7:66,247] provide acute crisis services in the community. Additionally, the Department is responsible for the maintenance of interior  

[6:8:66,257] finishes and equipment at Canyon Springs, a 57,000-square-foot leased facility in Riverside County. These facilities support the  

[6:9:66,267] Department's mission in providing medical, dental, and nursing care; active treatment; supervision; education; and vocational  

[6:10:66,277] training for residents with developmental disabilities committed to a state-operated facility.

[6:0:66,375] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,394] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION  

[7:0:66,411] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[7:1:66,421] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters  

[7:2:66,430] functions such as: policy development and management, program oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[7:3:66,440] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[8:0:66,457] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered  

[8:1:66,467] centrally from headquarters.  

[9:0:66,484] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,502] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[10:1:66,512] services to patients admitted into its system of care. Headquarters Administration includes headquarters functions such as:  

[10:2:66,521] policy development and management, healthcare standards compliance, statewide patients' rights coordination, clinical  

[10:3:66,531] oversight, data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[10:4:66,548] 4400020 - HOSPITAL ADMINISTRATION  

[11:0:66,566] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters includes a Hospital Administration component. Hospital Administration includes  

[11:1:66,575] centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care in DSH hospitals but are administered centrally from  

[11:2:66,585] headquarters such as: technology services, hospital police and fire oversight, patient referral management, clinical recruitment,  

[11:3:66,595] patient benefit and billing management, and Medicare revenue collection.  

[11:4:66,612] 4410 - STATE HOSPITALS  

[12:0:66,630] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[12:1:66,639] Patton. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to  

[12:2:66,649] those with serious mental illness and are   predominantly ordered for treatment by a criminal or civil court or by the Board of  

[12:3:66,659] Parole Hearings. To a lesser extent, the Department of State Hospitals also receives referrals for state hospital treatment from  

[12:4:66,669] county behavioral health departments or the public guardians, as well as from the California Department of Corrections and  

[12:5:66,678] Rehabilitation (CDCR). The state hospitals treat the following types of patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-

[12:6:66,688] Short Act (LPS); forensic commitments such as Incompetent to Stand Trial (IST), Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity (NGI),  

[12:7:66,698] Sexually Violent Predators (SVP), and Offender with a Mental Health Disorder (OMD); and prisoners with mental illness  

[12:8:66,708] ( Coleman ) from CDCR.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] 4410010 - ATASCADERO  

[4:0:66,86] The Department of State Hospitals-Atascadero opened in 1954 and is located on the Central Coast of California in Atascadero  

[4:1:66,96] (San Luis Obispo County). The hospital is a self-contained psychiatric hospital constructed within a security perimeter. The  

[4:2:66,105] majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for treatment by   Superior Courts or by CDCR pursuant to various  

[4:3:66,115] sections of the California Penal Code   and the Welfare and Institutions Code.  

[4:4:66,132] DSH-Atascadero primarily serves the following four patient types: OMD,  Coleman   patients from CDCR, IST, and   NGI.  

[4:5:66,150] 4410020 - COALINGA  

[5:0:66,167] The Department of State Hospitals-Coalinga opened in 2005 and is located on the western edge of Fresno County. The  

[5:1:66,177] hospital is California’s newest forensic mental health hospital and was created to primarily treat SVPs. It is a self-contained  

[5:2:66,186] psychiatric hospital constructed with a security perimeter. CDCR provides perimeter security as well as transportation of  

[5:3:66,196] patients to outside medical services and court proceedings. The majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for  

[5:4:66,206] treatment by   Superior Courts or CDCR pursuant to various sections of the California Penal Code and the Welfare and  

[5:5:66,216] Institutions Code.  

[5:6:66,233] DSH-Coalinga primarily serves SVP, OMD and  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[5:7:66,250] 4410030 - METROPOLITAN  

[6:0:66,268] The Department of State Hospitals-Metropolitan opened in 1916 and is located in Norwalk (Los Angeles County). The hospital  

[6:1:66,277] is an open style campus with a security perimeter. Due to concerns raised by the community, DSH-Metropolitan maintains a  

[6:2:66,287] formal agreement with the City of Norwalk and the Los Angeles County Sheriff not to accept patients charged with murder or a  

[6:3:66,297] sex crime, or that are at high risk for escape.  

[6:4:66,314] DSH-Metropolitan primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[6:5:66,331] 4410040 - NAPA  

[7:0:66,349] The Department of State Hospitals-Napa opened in 1875 and is located in Napa County. The hospital   was the first of the  

[7:1:66,359] five   State Hospitals and is   the oldest California state hospital still in operation.   It has an open style campus with a security  

[7:2:66,368] perimeter.  

[8:0:66,386] DSH-Napa primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[8:1:66,403] 4410050 - PATTON  

[9:0:66,420] The Department of State Hospitals-Patton opened in 1893 and is located in San Bernardino County. The hospital has an open  

[9:1:66,430] style campus with a security perimeter. CDCR correctional officers provide perimeter security and transportation at DSH-Patton  

[9:2:66,440] as well as transportation of patients to outside medical services and some court proceedings.  

[9:3:66,457] DSH-Patton primarily serves the following five patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, NGI and female  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[9:4:66,474] 4410060 - HOSPITAL POLICE OFFICER ACADEMY  

[9:5:66,491] The Department of State Hospitals Police Officer Academy is overseen by the Office of Protective Services, which is a full  

[9:6:66,501] service law enforcement agency that protects the safety and security of the state hospital facilities, staff and patients. The  

[9:7:66,511] Department provides training standards, model programs, cultural competency, program development, and a comprehensive  

[9:8:66,521] training plan to all protective services staff. 

[9:9:66,538] 4420 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[9:10:66,558] The Conditional Release Program is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic patients.  

[9:11:66,567] Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations on  

[9:12:66,577] January 1, 1986.  

[9:13:66,594] 4420010 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,612] The Conditional Release Program General/Non-Sexually Violent Predators is comprised of   NGI, OMD, and IST. Individuals  

[10:1:66,621] suitable for this program may be recommended by the state hospital medical director to the courts for outpatient treatment.  

[10:2:66,631] Currently, DSH contracts with county-operated and private organizations   serving all 58 counties in the state with non-SVP  

[10:3:66,641] commitments.  

[11:0:66,658] 4420020 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM -   SEXUALLY VIOLENT PREDATORS  

[11:1:66,676] The Conditional Release Program-Sexually Violent Predators was added to the Conditional Release Program effective January  

[11:2:66,685] 1, 1996 per Welfare and Institutions Code 6604. Prior to the conditional release of the first   SVP in 2003,   conditional release  

[11:3:66,695] providers did not have treatment services that would allow them to accept sexually violent predators as patients, requiring the  

[11:4:66,705] Department of State Hospitals to enter into an annual contract with a single private provider serving 58 counties. Current  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] statute requires SVPs be conditionally released to their county of domicile and sufficient funding be available to provide

[3:2:66,96] 4430 - CONTRACTED PATIENT SERVICES

[4:2:66,132] Treatment programs, IST Diversion programs, Community-Based Restoration programs and Community Inpatient Facility  

[4:3:66,142] programs.  

[5:0:66,159] 4430030 - OTHER CONTRACTED SERVICES  

[6:0:66,177] The Other Contracted Services includes additional contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its  

[6:1:66,186] patients outside of state hospital facilities. Programs include IST Diversion and Community-Based Restoration programs. 

[6:2:66,204] 4430040 - The Other Contracted Services focuses on policy development, program management and oversight of Jail Based  

[6:3:66,213] Treatment Programs and Community Based IST Programs.  

[7:0:66,231] 4430050 - The Jail Based Treatment Programs focus on defendants deemed IST on felony charges and provides mental health  

[7:1:66,241] treatment to these individuals in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court proceedings.  

[7:2:66,258] 4430060 - The Community Based Incompetent to Stand Trial programs are partnerships with various counties to treat felony  

[7:3:66,268] IST in a community mental health treatment setting. This includes Community-Based Restoration, Diversion and Community  

[7:4:66,277] Inpatient Facilities.  

[8:0:66,295] 4450 - Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the   Offender with a Mental Health Disorder and the Sex Offender  

[8:1:66,304] Commitment Programs as well as the Incompetent to Stand Trial Re-Evaluation Services program.  

[8:2:66,322] 4450010 - The Department is required to provide forensic evaluation services to determine if an inmate within the California  

[8:3:66,331] Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation, prior to parole, requires continued treatment in a state hospital as an Offender  

[8:4:66,341] with a Mental Health Disorder or as a Sexually Violent Predator as a condition of parole. The Department administers these  

[8:5:66,351] services through the Offender with a Mental Health Disorder Program and the Sex Offender Commitment Program.  

[8:6:66,368] 4450020 - The Re-Evaluation Services for Felony Incompetent to Stand Trial program allows the Department to re-evaluate  

[8:7:66,378] individuals deemed felony IST, who have been waiting in jail pending transfer to a Department restoration of competency  

[8:8:66,388] program.

[3:0:66,69] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[4:0:66,87] The Department of State Hospitals oversees five hospitals (Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan, Napa, and Patton State  

[4:1:66,97] Hospitals) that have a campus infrastructure comprising more than 6.6 million square feet of space on 2,600 acres of land.  

[4:2:66,107] These facilities aid in the Department’s mission to provide evaluation and treatment services in a safe and responsible manner  

[4:3:66,117] to State Hospital patients.

[5:0:66,138] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,157] 4170 - The Commission, established in 2004, provides oversight and accountability for portions of the Mental Health Services  

[6:1:66,167] Act (MHSA), Adult and Older Adult System of Care Act, Children’s Mental Health Services Act, and Mental Health Student  

[6:2:66,177] Services Act. The Commission’s primary roles include:  

[6:3:66,194] Program Review, Oversight and Accountability  

[7:0:66,211] The Commission provides oversight, review, training, technical assistance, accountability, and evaluation of specified mental  

[7:1:66,221] health projects and programs supported with MHSA funds.   This includes review and approval of county mental health  

[7:2:66,231] Innovation Programs   and Expenditure Plans.   It also includes assessing whether services that are provided pursuant to the  

[7:3:66,241] MHSA are cost-effective and in accordance with recommended best practices.  

[7:4:66,258] Policy Projects 

[8:0:66,275] The Commission may advise the Governor and the Legislature regarding actions the state may take to improve care and  

[8:1:66,285] services for   individuals living   with mental illness. The Commission executes projects designed to inform mental health policy by  

[8:2:66,295] integrating research findings and experiential knowledge. The Commission’s projects include criminal justice mental health, the  

[8:3:66,304] state suicide prevention plan, workplace mental health standards, prevention and early intervention strategies, and school-

[8:4:66,314] based mental health.  

[8:5:66,331] Strategic Partnerships  

[9:0:66,349] The Commission partners with universities, institutes, and public agencies to develop, field-test and implement changes and  

[9:1:66,359] policy solutions. The Commission’s partnerships include the Full Service Partnership Pilot, the Early Psychosis Learning Health  

[9:2:66,368] Care Network, the Youth Innovation Project, the Innovation Incubator project, and the suicide crisis center project.  

[9:3:66,386] Grant Programs  

[10:0:66,403] The Commission manages grant programs that incentivize stronger partnerships, integrated services, braided funding and the  

[10:1:66,413] evaluation required for continuous improvement. The Commission’s grant programs include the Mental Health Wellness Act of  

[10:2:66,422] 2013 crisis prevention, early intervention, and crisis response grants, youth drop-in centers, the early psychosis project, and the  

[10:3:66,432] Mental Health Student Services Act.

[9:0:66,430] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:1:66,449] 4181 - ENERGY PROGRAMS  

[10:0:66,466] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through  

[10:1:66,476] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization, and renewable energy services.  

[10:2:66,493] The Low Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households  

[10:3:66,503] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related  

[10:4:66,512] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard  

[10:5:66,522] the health and safety of household occupants.  

[11:0:66,549] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[11:1:66,559] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants.  

[11:2:66,576] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides energy efficiency and renewable energy services in low-income  

[11:3:66,586] single-family farmworker and multi-family dwellings to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and lower energy costs. LIWP  

[11:4:66,596] projects include weatherization and solar photovoltaic system installations.  

[11:5:66,613] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES  

[12:0:66,630] The Community Services Block Grant (CSBG) is designed to enable local government and nonprofit community organizations  

[12:1:66,640] to help low-income families achieve and maintain economic security through a broad range of activities. These activities include  

[12:2:66,650] education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health and nutritional  

[12:3:66,660] services, among others.  

[13:0:66,677] The California Earned Income Tax Credit (CalEITC) benefits low-income, working Californians by providing cash-back tax  

[13:1:66,687] credits to boost the income of eligible individuals and families. Since 2017-18,   the Department   has worked with the Franchise  

[13:2:66,697] Tax Board to provide grant opportunities for community-based organizations to increase awareness of CalEITC and free tax  

[13:3:66,706] preparation assistance programs.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] Covered California's mission is to increase the number of insured Californians, improve health care quality, lower costs, and  

[3:1:66,78] reduce health disparities through an innovative, competitive marketplace that empowers consumers to choose the health plan  

[3:2:66,88] and providers that give them the best value.

[4:1:66,117] Legislature. Per Government Code section 100503(o), the board authorizes a budget to pay program expenses from the  

[4:2:66,127] California Health Trust Fund to administer the Exchange.

[0:0:66,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — HHS   162 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,101] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to individuals with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,111] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state so that individuals with  

[5:2:66,121] disabilities may prepare for and engage in competitive integrated employment and achieve economic self-sufficiency. In  

[5:3:66,130] addition, the Department has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (secondary and postsecondary education,  

[5:4:66,140] behavioral/mental health, and welfare) to provide services to consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of  

[5:5:66,150] Selection process, which gives priority to individuals with the most significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,167] Individuals with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range  

[6:1:66,177] of services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement,  

[6:2:66,187] supported employment and independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their  

[6:3:66,196] communities. The Department provides Work Incentives Planning services to reduce dependency on public benefits. The  

[6:4:66,206] Department provides career counseling and information and referral services to encourage individuals working in non-

[6:5:66,216] competitive, non-integrated settings to work toward and achieve competitive integrated employment.  

[7:0:66,233] The Department additionally provides pre-employment transition student services, known as DOR Student Services, and  

[7:1:66,243] auxiliary aids and services necessary to participate in such services to a wide range of students with disabilities, ages 16 up to  

[7:2:66,253] 22 (depending on their exit from their special education program), including many who may benefit from early career  

[7:3:66,263] development. DOR Student Services include job exploration counseling, work-based learning experiences, postsecondary  

[7:4:66,272] education counseling, workplace readiness training, and instruction in self-advocacy. 

[8:0:66,290] The Department, through its Business Enterprises Program, provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to  

[8:1:66,299] enable individuals who are blind or visually impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and  

[8:2:66,309] cafeterias. Prevocational, including employment readiness, services are provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to  

[8:3:66,319] consumers with vision loss to prepare them for independent living.  

[9:0:66,336] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[9:1:66,346] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[9:2:66,356] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[10:0:66,373] The   Department administers the Pathways to Success Project (PSP) to increase competitive integrated employment outcomes,  

[10:1:66,383] economic self-sufficiency, independence, and inclusion, through a unique service delivery design supported by sector-specific  

[10:2:66,393] teams specializing in high-wage, high-skill, and high-demand careers for individuals with disabilities. The PSP, which is a pilot  

[10:3:66,402] research project, is particularly targeted at underrepresented communities, including people of color, women, and individuals  

[10:4:66,412] with intellectual or developmental disabilities. 

[11:0:66,429] The Department administers the California Subminimum Wage to Competitive Integrated Employment Project (CSP) to provide  

[11:1:66,439] a comprehensive set of interventions and supports to increase competitive integrated employment outcomes, independence,  

[11:2:66,449] economic self-sufficiency, and inclusion for individuals with the most significant disabilities currently in, or contemplating  

[11:3:66,459] entering, subminimum wage employment. The CSP, which is a pilot research project, will establish evidence-based approaches  

[11:4:66,469] to vocational rehabilitation service delivery that will improve the employment outcomes of its participants, transitioning more  

[11:5:66,478] workers with disabilities into competitive integrated employment. 

[12:0:66,496] The Department administers the Integrated Employment in Recovery program (IER) to provide training to the provider  

[12:1:66,505] workforce on evidence-based practices to serve people with substance use disorders (SUD) related to opioid use that can be  

[12:2:66,515] incorporated as a part of holistic recovery. The training focuses on incorporating the full range of vocational rehabilitation  

[12:3:66,525] services into treatment delivery as part of a whole-person approach to recovery and developing supports for individuals  

[12:4:66,535] returning to or transitioning into work during and following treatment. 

[13:0:66,552] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[14:0:66,569] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[14:1:66,579] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[14:2:66,589] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[14:3:66,599] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[14:4:66,608] services to community-based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[15:0:66,626] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[15:1:66,635] families, six service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for individuals with  

[15:2:66,645] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[15:3:66,655] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. The Department also works with the federal government to  

[15:4:66,665] administer a TBI partnership grant with which a state TBI Advisory Board has been established for the purpose of creating a  

[15:5:66,675] TBI state plan, sustainability plan, statewide TBI registry, and needs assessment.  

[16:0:66,692] In addition, the Department expands the capacity of existing TBI sites and stands up new TBI sites in alignment with Home and  

[16:1:66,702] Community-Based Services surrounding transition and diversion through community reintegration, personal care services  

[16:2:66,711] through supported living services, and other supportive services to improve functional capabilities of individuals with TBI.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 16 non-profit community-based  

[3:1:66,78] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[3:2:66,88] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[3:3:66,98] vision evaluations/screenings, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills,  

[3:4:66,108] independent living skills training, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[3:5:66,125] Through a partnership with the California Public Utilities Commission’s Deaf and Disabled Telecommunications Program, the  

[3:6:66,135] Department’s Voice Options program provides eligible Californians who are unable to speak, or who have difficulty speaking,  

[3:7:66,144] with a free speech-generating device. The goal of this program is to ensure full and equal telephone communications access  

[3:8:66,154] for all Californians with disabilities.  

[4:0:66,171] The Department administers the Community Living Fund program that provides   transition or diversion services to individuals to  

[4:1:66,181] support community-based living which enables older adults and people with disabilities to access funding to move from an  

[4:2:66,191] institutional setting to the community or to support individuals who are at risk of going into an institution to remain in their  

[4:3:66,201] community.  

[4:4:66,218] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[5:0:66,238] The Administration Program provides overall management planning, policy development, and administrative support services  

[5:1:66,247] to departmental programs. This program and the related distributed administration will no longer be displayed beginning in  

[5:2:66,257] 2023-24.

[2:0:144,32] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,84] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,101] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing  

[4:1:66,111] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[4:2:66,121] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,130] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[4:4:66,140] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[4:5:66,157] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[5:0:66,175] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[5:1:66,184] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[5:2:66,194] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[5:3:66,211] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[6:0:66,229] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[6:1:66,239] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[6:2:66,248] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[6:3:66,258] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[6:4:66,268] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[6:5:66,278] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[6:6:66,287] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.
